Jamison Brereton

32 (266)
Indra
Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra G─Бthina
17 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
The ritual application of this hymn is announced in the first verse: the Midday Pressing of soma, which in some ritual circles, as here, Indra shares with the Marut troop, his supporters in the Vr╠еtra battle. Throughout the hymn invitations to drink soma at this rite are interspersed with praises of IndraтАЩs cosmogonic deeds, espe
cially the slaying of Vr╠еtra. In verses 9тАУ10 IndraтАЩs powers are ascribed to his origi nal drinking of soma immediately after birth, with the implicit suggestion that the sacrificersтАЩ current offering of soma will revitalize those powers for the sacrificersтАЩ benefit.
For the most part the language of this hymn is straightforward and even a bit monotonous, and there are a number of technical terms pertaining to the soma sacrifice (see, e.g., the types of soma in vs. 2). There are, however, several studied contrastive pairs (e.g., тАЬvulnerable…invulnerable,тАЭ vs. 4; тАЬgoddesses…godless,тАЭ vs. 6; see also vss. 7, 11), as well as a few striking images, such as Indra тАЬwearing the earth on his other hipтАЭ (vs. 11) as an indication of his greatness.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, lord of the Soma, drink this Soma which is grateful to you at noon-day sacrifice, Maghavan, partake of the spiritless Soma, unyoke your horses, and filling their jaws (with fodder), exhilarate them at this ceremony.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

O Indra, lord of soma, drink this soma here, the Midday Pressing, which is dear to you.
Snuffling out your two lips, you bounteous possessor of the silvery drink, having unhitched your two fallow bays, reach exhilaration here.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The impv. p├нba is accented, though it is located mid-clause. There is no obvious reason for this. Oldenberg suggests weakly (ZDMG 60: 736) that it is an emphatic accent, but this is of course a circular argument: any verb bearing an unexpected accent can be called emphatic. I find the accent esp. disturbing because the identical phrase, minus the initial voc. ├нndra, is found without accented impv. elsewhere: #s├│mam somapate piba# (V.40.1=VIII.21.3) versus our #├нndra s├│maс╣Г somapate p├нbem├бm#. There are several possible contributing factors. First, three p─Бdas at the beginning of this hymn begin with accented p├нb─Б (2b, 3d, 5b), and our form may have had its accent added redactionally. However, I think that p├нba has special status and can be accented in positions that strict syntactic rules would not allow. (This is rather like OldenbergтАЩs тАЬemphaticтАЭ argument, except that I limit the effect to a single verb form.) See esp. I.15.1, II.37.1-3 and comm. there. The unsanctioned accent may arise partly because p├нba тАШdrink!тАЩ is a particularly rousing verb in RVic discourse. It also often occurs in non-initial position when it nonetheless legitimately has accent – after init. vocatives (e.g. ├нndra p├нba III.36.2, etc.) or at the beginning of a clause after another short clause (or clauses) (e.g., VIII.4.8 t┼л╠Бyam ├йhi dr├бv─Б p├нba тАЬCome here swiftly! Run! Drink!тАЭ), and this may have led to the sense that it can be accented in non-initial position in general. I also note in LubotskyтАЩs conspectus that unaccented piba generally occupies either final position in its p─Бda or second position, while accented p├нba, besides being common and expected in initial position, tends to avoid both those positions except when 2nd position follows an initial voc. (as in III.36.2, etc.) or final position opens a new clause (as in VIII.4.8). Note that if this distribution holds, the тАЬidenticalтАЭ phrases I cite at the beginning of this comment are not the same after all, because unaccented piba is p─Бda-final and our accented p├нba is followed by another element. However, there are a few counterexamples with p─Бda-final piba╠З not beginning a new clause (e.g., VIII.4.3, 65.5). One can speculate on why 2nd and final position would favor the unaccented verb while full medial favors the accented form: namely, that 2nd position is of course WackernagelтАЩs position, where enclitics typically migrate, and, assuming a basic SOV underlying order, absolute final position is the default position for unaccented main-clause verbs. Still, the full medial position where we find accented main-clause p├нba does not otherwise favor or impose accent on other verbs that appear there, so if this hypothesis holds, it is only for this special verb.

Geldner rather charmingly suggests that prapr├║thya represents тАЬbrr machendтАЭ to stop the horses. Although тАЬwhoaтАЭ would be the equivalent English word/vocal gesture, given the object тАШlipsтАЩ (┼Ы├нpre), I wonder if itтАЩs the тАЬhorse training voice commandтАЭ (gleaned on the internet) called тАЬsmoochingтАЭ – defined as тАЬkissing sound with lips used to ask a horse to move on or up a gait.тАЭ I rather like the idea of Indra smooching to his fallow bays.

Griffith

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, drink the Soma mixed with milk, with butter-milk, or fresh; we offer it for your exhilaration, associated with the devout company of the Maruts and the Rudras; drink it till you are satisfied.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Mixed with milk: gava┼Ыiram, manthinam, ┼Ыukram: manthinam = manthasaс╣Гyuktam, mixed with butter-milk;

┼Ъukram = abhinavan, new or fresh; or, the terms may mean ┼Ыukramanthigrahe vartam─Бnam, being in the vessel of acid butter-milk;

Devout: brahmakс╣Ыt─Б = indrastotram kurv─Бс╣Зena, making the praise of Indra

Jamison Brereton

Mixed with cows [=milk], stirred (with meal), or pure, o IndraтАФdrink the soma. We have given it to you for your exhilaration.
Joined in pleasure with the formulation-making flock of Maruts, with the Rudras, drench yourself (in it), to satiety.

Griffith

Quaff it pure, meal-blent, mixt with milk, O Indra; we have poured forth the Soma for thy rapture.
Knit with the prayer-fulfilling band of Maruts, yea, with the Rudras, drink till thou art sated;

Geldner

Trink, Indra, den milchgemischten, den mit Mehl anger├╝hrten, den klaren Soma! Wir haben ihn dir zum Rausche gespendet. Zusammen mit der marutischen Gefolgschaft, die dir eine Erbauung bereitet, mit den Rudras├╢hnen begie├Яe dich zur Gen├╝ge!

Grassmann

Den milchgemischten Soma, den gequirlten, den reinen trink, den dir zum Rausch wir gaben, Mit deiner frommen Marutschar, o Indra, der Rudraschar vereinigt schwelge lustig,

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThese are the Maruts, Indra, who, worshipping your prowess, augment your withering force (by their aid); attended by the Rudras, drink, wielder of the thunder-bolt, and handsome-chinned, at the noon-day sacrifice.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

They who increased your tempestuousness, who increased your power, the Maruts, hymning your strength, IndraтАФ
at the Midday Pressing, you with mace in hand, drink in a flock with the Rudras, you of good lips.

Griffith

Those who gave increase to thy strength and vigour; the Maruts singing forth thy might, O Indra.
Drink thou, O fair of cheek, whose hand wields thunder, with Rudras banded, at our noon libation.

Geldner

Die Marut, die deine Wut, deine Kraft erh├╢hten, indem sie deine St├дrke besangen, o Indra, mit den Rudras├╢hnen als Gefolge trink, du Sch├╢nlippiger, bei der mitt├дglichen Trankspende, du Keulentr├дger!

Grassmann

Die deinen Muth und deine Kraft erquickten die Maruts, Indra, deine St├дrke preisend; Blitzhalter trinke bei der Mittagsspende, o Schl├╝rfender, vereint mit Rudrascharen.

Elizarenkova

рдпреЗ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рд╢рд░реНрдзрдГ рдмрд▓рднреВрддрд╛рдГ рдЖрд╕рдиреН рддреЗ рдЗрддреН рдд рдПрд╡ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдп ред рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрд╛рд░реНрдереЗ рд╖рд╖реНрдареА ред рдЗрдордорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдВ рдордзреБрдорддреН ред рддрд╡ рд╕рд╣рд╛рдпрд╛ рд╡рдпрдорд╛рд╕реНрдорд╣реЗ рддреНрд╡рдВ рдпреБрджреНрдзрдорднрд┐рдЧрдЪреНрдЫреЗрддрд┐ рдорд╛рдзреБрд░реНрдпреЛрдкреЗрддрдВ рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрдВ рдпрдерд╛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рддрдерд╛ рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░реЗ рдиреБ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдВ рдкреНрд░реИрд░рдпрдиреН ред рдпреЗрднрд┐рдГ рдпреИрд░реНрдпреБрджреНрдзрд╕рд╣рд╛рдпреИрд░реНрдорд░реБрджреНрднрд┐рдГ рдЗрд╖рд┐рддрдГ рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рд┐рдд рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдЕрдорд░реНрдордгрдГ рдкрд░реИрдГ рдЕрд╡рд┐рджрд┐рддрдорд░реНрдорд╕реНрдерд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рдЕрдд рдПрд╡ рдордиреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рди рдХреЛрд╜рдкрд┐ рдордо рд╣рдиреНрддреЗрддреНрдпрднрд┐рдордиреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рдЕрд╕реБрд░рд╕реНрдп рдорд░реНрдо рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╣реГрддреМ рд╕рддреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╕ рдорд░рд┐рд╖реНрдпрддрд┐ рддрд╛рджреГрд╢рдВ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдирдВ рд╡рд┐рд╡реЗрдж рдЕрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рд╕реАрддреН рее рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░реЗ ред тАШ рд╡рд┐рдк рдХреНрд╖реЗрдкрдгреЗ ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд▓рд┐рдЯрд┐ рд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпреЗрдирд╛рддреНрдордиреЗрдкрджрдореН ред рдЗрд░реЗрдЪрдГ тАв рдЗрд░рдпреЛ рд░реЗ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд░реЗ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреЗрд╢рдГ ред рдирд┐рдШрд╛рддрдГрее рдЖрд╕рдиреН ред’ рдЕрд╕ рднреБрд╡рд┐ ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд▓рдЩрд┐ рд░реВрдкрдореН ред рдпрджреНрд╡реГрддреНрддрдпреЛрдЧрд╛рдиреНрдирд┐рдШрд╛рддрд╛рднрд╛рд╡рдГ ред рд╡рд┐рд╡реЗрдж ред тАШ рд╡рд┐рдж рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдиреЗ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд▓рд┐рдЯрд┐ рд░реВрдкрдореН ред рд▓рд┐рддреНрд╕реНрд╡рд░рдГ ред рдорд░реНрдо ред’ рдореГрдЩреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрддреНрдпрд╛рдЧреЗ ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рджреМрдгрд╛рджрд┐рдХреЛ рдордирд┐рдиреН ред рдирд┐рддреНрд╕реНрд╡рд░рдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThose were the Maruts who were the strength of Indra, and genitive ly encouraged him; animated by whom he pierced the vital part of Vс╣Ыtra, fancying himself vulnerable.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

It was they who became inspired at his honeyed (drink), IndraтАЩs troop, who were the Maruts,
impelled by whom he found the vulnerable place of Vr╠еtra, who thought himself invulnerable.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner (and in part Renou) take m├бdhumat as referring to speech (тАЬтАж wurden beredt in s├╝ssen (Worten)тАЭ), but though m├бdhumant- occurs several times with v├бcas- and the noun v├нpra- тАШinspired poetтАЩ demonstrates that тИЪvip тАШbecome inspiredтАЩ can have a strong verbal component, still the focus of this hymn is soma – and the default referent of m├бdhumant- тАШhoneyedтАЩ is soma. Here the underlying word must be neut. (which s├│ma- of course is not), but the neut. s├бvana- тАШpressingтАЩ is found elsewhere with this adj. (cf. X.112.7 m├бdhumattam─Бni тАж s├бvan─Б), and s├бvana- is found three times in the first five vss. of this hymn (1b, 3c, 5a). Note the insistent repetition of ma in p─Бda d (amarm├бс╣Зo m├бnyam─Бnasya m├бrma), anticipated by m├бdhumad in a and mar├║taс╕е in b, and continued by the first word in 5a manuс╣гv├бd. This phonetic figure may be signaling the MarutsтАЩ name. See also vs. 7.

Griffith

They, even the Maruts who were there, excited with song the meath-created strength of Indra.
By them impelled to act he reached the vitals Of Vrtra, though he deemed that none might wound him.

Geldner

Eben diese seine Gef├дhrten wurden beredt in s├╝├Яen Worten, die Marut, die des Indra Truppe waren, von denen zur Eile getrieben er des Vritra verwundbare Stelle fand, der sich f├╝r unverwundbar hielt.

Grassmann

Sie wirbelten hinein das S├╝ss des Soma’s, die Maruts, die des Indra Heerbann waren, Mit denen eilend er durchstiess die Weichen des Vritra, der sich unverwundbar d├╝nkte.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ рд▓реЛрдЧ рдзрди рдЖрджрд┐ рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдп рд╕реЗ рд╕рдмрдХреЗ рд╕реБрдЦ рдХреА рд╡реГрджреНрдзрд┐ рдФрд░ рджреБрдГрдЦреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рдХреЗ рд╕рдмрд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╕рдиреНрди рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рдЙрдирдХреЛ рд╣реА рдзрд╛рд░реНрдорд┐рдХ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдорд╛рдирдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ реерекрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдпреЗ рдорд░реБрддреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдпреЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рд╢рд░реНрджреНрдзреЛ рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░реЗ рдЖрд╕рдиреНрдордзреБрдорджрд┐рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░реЗ рдпреЛ рдпреЗрднрд┐рд░рд┐рд╖рд┐рддреЛ рд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдпреЗрд╡рд╛рд╜рдорд░реНрдордгреЛ рдорд░реНрдо рдордиреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рд╡реЗрдж рддреЗ рд╕ рдЪ рдиреБ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рднреАрд╖реНрдЯрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ реерекрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирдГ рдХреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕реЛ рднрд╡рдиреНрддреАрддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рддреЗ) рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЛрдХреНрддрд╛рдГ (рдЗрддреН) рдПрд╡ (рдиреБ) рд╕рджреНрдпрдГ (рдЕрд╕реНрдп) рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп (рдордзреБрдорддреН) рдмрд╣реВрдирд┐ рдордзреБрд░рд╛рджрд┐рдЧреБрдгрдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдирд┐ рд╡рд╕реНрддреВрдирд┐ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдБрд╕реНрддрддреН (рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░реЗ) рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкрдиреНрддрд┐ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп) рдкрд░рдореИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдпреБрдХреНрддрд╕реНрдп (рд╢рд░реНрдзрдГ) рдмрд▓рдореН (рдорд░реБрддрдГ) рд╡рд╛рдпрд╡ рдЗрд╡ рд╡реЗрдЧрдмрд▓рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдГ (рдпреЗ) (рдЖрд╕рдиреН) рдЖрд╕реНрдпреЗ (рдпреЗрднрд┐рдГ) рдпреИрдГ (рд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп) рдореЗрдШрд╕реНрдпреЗрд╡ рд╢рддреНрд░реЛрдГ (рдЗрд╖рд┐рддрдГ) рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рд┐рддрдГ (рд╡рд┐рд╡реЗрдж) рд╡рд┐рдЬрд╛рдиреАрдпрд╛рддреН (рдЕрдорд░реНрдордгрдГ) рдЕрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдВ рдорд░реНрдо рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдВрд╕реНрддрд╕реНрдп (рдордиреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп) рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддреБрдГ (рдорд░реНрдо) рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдкреНрд░рд╣рддреЗ рдореНрд░рд┐рдпрддреЗ рддрддреН реерекрее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPhased with the sacrifice, as if it was that of Manu, drink, Indra, the Soma, for the sake of perpetual vigour; come, lord of the tawny steeds, with the adorable Maruts, and with the traversers (of the air); send down the waters (of the firmament) to (blend with) the waters of the earth.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Send down the waters: apo arс╣З─Б sisaс╣Ыsi = antarikс╣гasthit─Бn yudak─Бni p─Бrthiv─Бn yudak─Бni, pr─Бpaya, cause the waters staying in mid-air to reach, or become those of, earth

Jamison Brereton

As by Manu, o Indra, enjoying the pressing, drink the soma for manly power ever new.
Let yourself be turned hither by our sacrifices, you of the fallow bays. Along with the hastening ones, you set to running the flooding
waters,

Jamison Brereton Notes

The rendering of vavс╣Ыtsva in the published translation (тАЬlet yourself be turned hitherтАЭ), a sort of passive reflexive, now seems over-elaborate to me; I would substitute тАЬbe turned.тАЭ The other examples of this mid. pf. impv. seem more straightforwardly simply тАЬturnтАЭ or тАЬturn yourself,тАЭ but if yaj├▒a├нс╕е has true instrumental force, a passive rendering is more natural. Possible, however, is RenouтАЩs тАЬgr├вce ├а (nos) sacrifices.тАЭ The referent of saraс╣Зy├║bhiс╕е is not totally clear. S─Бyaс╣Зa. (fld. by Renou) suggests the Maruts, while Geldner adds horses or waves as possibilities. The other ex. of a plural to this stem (also instr.) in I.62.4 is in a clear Vala context, with the Navagvas and Da┼Ыagvas in the same vs., which would suggest the Aс╣Еgirases – but, although the Vala myth and the Aс╣Еgirases were prominent in the preceding hymn III.31, they are not found in this hymn, which is dominated by the Maruts and which mentions only the Vс╣Ыtra myth (here and in the following vs.). I therefore think it likely that S─Бyaс╣Зa. was correct. Note that saraс╣Зy├║- тАж sisarс╣гi is an etym. figure, continued by s├бrtava├н in the next vs. (6b).

The rendering of the phrase ap├│ ├бrс╣З─Б as тАЬthe flooding watersтАЭ in the publ tr.

assumes an emendation to fem. pl. ├бrс╣З─Бс╕е, with Grassmann and numerous others (see Oldenberg), contra the Pp and not reflecting the expected sandhi of such a form, which should be ├бrс╣З─Бс╕е. As Oldenberg points out, the emendation is not nec.: ├бrс╣З─Б could easily be a neut. pl.

to the thematic stem ├бrс╣Зa-. In this case the tr. would better read тАЬthe waters, the floods.тАЭ

Griffith

Pleased, like a man, with our libation, Indra, drink, for enduring hero might, the Soma.
Lord of Bays, moved by sacrifice come hither: thou with the Swift Ones stirrest floods and waters.

Geldner

Wie bei Manu der Trankspende dich erfreuend trink, Indra, den Soma zu voller Kraft. La├Я dich, du Falbenfahrer, durch die Opfer herlenken. Du l├д├Яt die Wasserfluten mit den Eilenden laufen.

Grassmann

Gleich wie ein Mensch lass dir den Soma schmecken, und trink den Saft zu stets erneuter St├дrke, Durch Opfer wende her dich, Rosselenker, zu Wassers Fluten eilst du mit den schnellen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬInasmuch as you have slain with active strife the slumbering, darking, water-investing Vс╣Ыtra, you have let forth the bright waters like horses (rushing) into battle.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When you sent forth the waters, like steeds to run in a contestтАФhaving smashed Vr╠еtra,
who was lying still, with your moving weapon of death, o Indra, him having surrounded the goddesses, godless himself.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. appears to have no main clause. I take it as loosely attached to the preceding vs., while Geldner attaches it to the next one. Oldenberg (fld. by Witzel Got┼Н) disputes the Nebensatz analysis, pointing first to the odd doubly accented Pp. analysis of pr─Б╠Бsс╣Ыjaс╕е as pr├б ├бsс╣Ыjaс╕е: if the verb is accented, we would expect univerbation with the preverb and loss of the preverb accent. He instead suggests that y├бd is to be construed with the participial phrase vс╣Ыtr├бс╣Г jaghanv─Б╠Бn, as if it contained the finite verb jag├бntha – a mixed construction. I am in general reluctant to allow a subordinating conjunction to have domain over a participle, and in this particular case this assumption would further require bits of the main clause and the subordinate clause to be interwoven in a fashion unprecedented (as far as I know) even in RVic syntax: the major part of the subordinate clause would be plunked down between the object of the main verb, ap├бс╕е, and that verb (pr─Б╠Бsс╣Ыjat), and the 2nd half verse would consist of NPs modifying the object of the subordinate clause but following the end of the main clause. I do admit that the position of y├бd dha in p─Бda a suggests a close relation with the participial phrase, but I do not consider that position sufficient to override the arguments against that analysis.

The vs. contains several nice oppositions: ┼Ы├бy─Бnam тАж c├бrat─Б тАЬ(him) lying (still) with (your) moving (weapon)тАЭ and the etymological dev─л╠Бr ├бdevam тАЬthe goddesses, godless тАжтАЭ In addition note the etymological pun: vс╣Ыtr├бm тАж vavriv─Б╠Бс╣Гsam.

Griffith

When thou didst loose the streams to run like racers in the swift contest, having smitten Vrtra
With flying weapon where he lay, O Indra, and, godless, kept the Goddesses encompassed.

Da du die Gew├дsser loslie├Яest, um wie Renner im Wettkampf zu laufen, nachdem du den Vritra erschlagen hattest, o Indra, mit der beweglichen Waffe den Liegenden, den Ungott, der die g├╢ttlichen Gew├дsser eingeschlossen hatte.

Die Wasser liessest rinnen du im Wettlauf wie Renner, als den Vritra du erschlagen Mit raschem Streiche, Indra, ihn, der da lag, der gottlos rings die G├╢ttinnen gebannt hielt.

English translation:

тАЬTherefore we sacrifice with reverence to the vast and mighty Indra, who is adorable, undecaying, young; whose magnitude the unbounded heaven and earth have not measures, nor can measure.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let us sacrifice to Indra, increased through homage, lofty and towering, unaging and youthful,
whose greatness the two dear world-halves measured, but did not measure up to the greatness of him worthy of the sacrifice.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The ma- phonetic figure that dominated 4d returns in this vs.: cd тАж mam├бtur тАж, тАж mahim─Б╠Бnam mam─Б╠Бte. This figure is reinforced by the first words of p─Бda a, y├бj─Бma ├нn n├бmas─Б, and the uninterrupted sequence of -am acc. singulars in ab: тАж vс╣Ыddh├бm ├нndram, bс╣Ыh├бntam с╣Ыс╣гv├бm aj├бram y├║v─Бnam. Although a side-effect of the grammar, it is my impression that a skilled RVic poet would break the monotony of such a string – unless it served some other poetic purpose, here to provide the mirror-image -am to ma- and perhaps to evoke the Maruts.

The two forms of the perfect to тИЪm─Б тАШmeasureтАЩ in the 2nd hemistich, act.

mam├бtuс╕е and med. mam─Б╠Бte, share the same subj. and obj., with the 1st clause positive and the second negated. Clearly the poet is playing with two different senses of тИЪm─Б.

Grassmann, Geldner, and Oldenberg neatly convert the word play to тАЬmessenтАЭ (тАШmeasureтАЩ) versus тАЬermessenтАЭ (тАШgauge, grasp, realizeтАЩ)(or so I understand them). My тАЬmeasureтАЭ / тАЬmeasure up toтАЭ is a similar attempt whose purport is close to K├╝mmel (378) and Witzel Got┼Н: тАЬsich messen.тАЭ

Griffith

With reverence let us worship mighty Indra, great and sublime, eternal, everyouthful,
Whose greatness the dear world-halves have not measured, no, nor conceived the might of him the Holy.

Geldner

So verehren wir unter Verbeugung den erstarkten Indra, den hohen, reckenhaften, alterlosen, jugendlichen Indra, den opferw├╝rdigen, dessen Gr├╢├Яe beide lieben Welten gemessen, aber nicht ermessen haben.

Grassmann

Lasst dehmuthsvoll den Indra uns verehren, den hohen, grossen, hehren, ewig jungen, Dess Gr├╢sse beide liebe Welten massen, doch nicht ermassen, dess der hoch zu ehren.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAll the gods cannot detract from the many glorious exploits, and pious works of Indra; he who has upheld earth, and heaven, and the firmament, and who, the performer of great deeds, has engendered the sun and the dawn.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Many are the well-done deeds of Indra. The All Gods do not violate the commandments (of him),
who upholds earth and this heaven. Of wondrous power, he begot the sun and the dawn.

Griffith

Many are Indra’s nobly wrought achievements, and none of all the Gods transgress his statutes.
He beareth up this earth and heaven, and, doer of marvels, he begot the Sun and Morning.

Geldner

Des Indra viele Werke sind wohlgetan. Alle G├╢tter verfehlen nicht seine Gebote, der die Erde und diesen Himmel gefestigt hat; der Guteswirkende hat die Sonne, die Morgenr├╢te erzeugt.

Grassmann

Viel sind des Indra sch├╢n vollbrachte Werke; die G├╢tter alle st├╢ren sein Gesetz nicht, Der diesen Himmel und die Erde festhielt und herrlich schuf die Sonn’ und Morgenr├╢the.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDoer of no wrong, such was your true greatness, that as soon as born, you have quaffed the Soma; neither the heavens, nor days, nor months, nor years, resist the force of you who is mighty.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Undeceptive one, this greatness of yours is truly real: because, just born, you drank the soma,
not the heavens, Indra, nor the days, nor the months and years could obstruct the strength of you, the powerful one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The juxtaposition of adrogh├б- тАШundeceptiveтАЩ and saty├б- тАШreal, trueтАЩ is also found in III.14.6 adrogh├йс╣Зa v├бcas─Б saty├бm.

The standard tr. take p─Бdas a and b together, with cd separate. I think it makes more sense to take b with cd, as supplying the reason (IndraтАЩs early soma drinking) that he couldnтАЩt be obstructed.

The standard tr. also take dy─Б╠Бvaс╕е as тАШdaysтАЩ, whereas the published translation agrees with Hoffmann (Injunk. 242) in tr. тАШheavensтАЩ. The problem, as I saw it then, was its cooccurrence with ├бh─Б likewise тАШdaysтАЩ, which led to awkward duplication. However, I have now rethought this; the series of temporal expressions in this hemistich (├бh─Б, m─Б╠Бs─Бс╕е ┼Ыaradaс╕е) invites a temporal reading of dy─Б╠Бvaс╕е as well and makes тАЬheavensтАЭ seem out of place. In X.7.4. and 12.4 the two stems also co-occur and I tr. тАЬdaytimes and days.тАЭ I would now substitute that tr. here as well.

varanta here and in 16b is formally ambiguous; it can be either an injunctive or a subjunctive to the root aor. (see Hoffmann 239-40); Hoffmann takes it as a subjunctive. It does not work terribly well as either one; in both passages I tr. it as a preterital modal (тАЬcould obstructтАЭ), but this interpr. is not firmly based in the morphology. I sense that in this vs. and the next the poet is struggling to express a verbal category that isnтАЩt found in the Skt. verbal system, namely anteriority: modal anteriority here, temporal anteriority in 10cd.

Griffith

Herein, O Guileless One, is thy true greatness, that soon as born thou drankest up the Soma.
Days may not check the power of thee the Mighty, nor the nights, Indra, nor the months, nor autumns.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAs soon as born in the highest heaven, you have quaffed, Indra, the Soma for your exhilaration; and when you had pervaded the heaven and earth, you became the primary artificer (of creation).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You, Indra, just born, drank the soma for exhilaration in the highest distant heaven.
After you had entered heaven and earth, then you became the first to suckle the bard.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As just noted, this vs. contains an apparent attempt to express anteriority: the pluperfect ─Б╠Бvive┼Ы─лс╕е seems to function like an English pluperfect (rather than the standard Vedic plupf., a past tense to a presential perfect), to express an action that happened before the action of the main verb, an interpr. more or less endorsed by K├╝mmel (500).

Griffith

As soon as thou wast born in highest heaven thou drankest Soma to delight thee, Indra;
And when thou hadst pervaded earth and heaven thou wast the first supporter of the singer.

Geldner

Du trankst, eben geboren, sogleich den Soma im h├╢chsten Himmel zum Rausche, o Indra. Als du in beide Welten eingezogen warst, da wurdest du der erste Brotgeber der Dichter.

Grassmann

Geboren kaum, im h├╢chsten Himmel, trankest den Soma du, zum Rausche dir, o Indra; Als du hinein in beide Welten drangest, da warst du schon der alte Hort der S├дnger.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, from whom many are born; you who is vigorous have slain Ahi, enveloping the slumbering water and confiding in his prowess; yet the heaven apprehended not your greatness as you remained concealing the earth by on eof your flames.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

As you remained concealing: anyay─Б sphigy─Б kс╣г─Бm avasth─Б = ekataray─Б kaс╣нy─Б bh┼лmim avacch─Бdya tiс╣гс╣нhasi

Jamison Brereton

You smashed the serpent lying around the flood, displaying its strengthтАФyou powerfully born, as more powerful (than he).
Heaven did not come close to your greatness then, when you wore the earth on the other hip.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The standard tr. (save for Hoffmann, Injunk. 100, sim. to my interpr.) take тАж sphigy─Б╠Аkс╣г─Б╠Бm ├бvasth─Бс╕е as тАЬyou covered/ clothed the earth with your hip,тАЭ but the medial root pres. to тИЪvas means тАШwearтАЩ and takes an acc. of the garment rather than an acc. of the entity being clothed (the construction found with v─Бs├бya-). See the similar ex. at VIII.4.8 and the comm. there, as well as the similar sentiment found in I.173.6, where Indra wears Heaven and Earth as various accessories. The point of course is to emphasize IndraтАЩs vast size by making Earth (and Heaven) seem puny in comparison. A similar point was made in vs. 7d, as well as in the immediately preceding p─Бda 11c.

Griffith

Thou, puissant God, more mighty, slewest. Ahi showing his strength when couched around the waters.
The heaven itself attained not to thy greatness when with one hip of thine the earth was shadowed.

Geldner

Du erschlugst den Drachen, der die Flut umlagerte, der sich stark f├╝hlte, du Starkgeborener als der St├дrkere. Nicht kam da der Himmel deiner Gr├╢├Яe gleich, als du mit der anderen H├╝fte die Erde bedecktest.

Grassmann

Du schlugst die Schlange, die die Flut umringte die m├дcht’ge st├дrker du, o kraftgeborner; Nicht kam der Himmel gleich da deiner Gr├╢sse, als du die Erd’ mit einer H├╝fte decktest.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis our sacrifice, Indra, is your augmentation, for the rite in which the Soma is effused is acceptable to you do you who is deserving of worship protect the worshipper by (the efficacy of) the worship, and may this sacrifice strengthen your thunderbolt for the slaying of Ahi.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Since the sacrifice has become your strengthener, Indra, and the dear ritual meal of pressed soma also, aid sacrifice upon sacrifice, being the one who deserves the sacrifice; the sacrifice aided your mace in the serpent-smashing.

Jamison Brereton Notes

yaj├▒├б- is the focus of this vs., with 5 occurrences of it or a transparent deriv.

I take v├бrdhanaс╕е as the predicate of p─Бda b as well as p─Бda a (тАЬthe meal is also your strengthenerтАЭ); the standard tr. take b as an independent nominal clause with priy├бс╕е as its predicate (тАЬthe meal is dear to youтАЭ). There is no way to tell for certain; the absence of te in b gives some support to my interpr., but that support is undeniably weak. The difference between the two tr. is also not large and has no effects on the interpr. of the rest of the vs. The second hemistich expresses the reciprocity of the sacrificial enterprise, neatly shown by the balanced verb forms to the same root тИЪav тАШaid, helpтАЩ: impv. ava (c), impf. ─Бvat (d). But the reciprocity is curiously indirect: Indra is asked to aid the sacrifice (rather than the sacrificer[s]), and the sacrifice aided IndraтАЩs mace (not Indra himself). In both clauses the direct object is an inanimate entity standing in for an animate one, and in the second clause the subject is inanimate as well. Only Indra is animate and capable of acting.

The nom. sg. pres. part. s├бn тАШbeingтАЩ is not used concessively (тАЬalthough being тАжтАЭ) as it normally is. I think it may have the same force as it does in III.30.5, a тАЬdefinitionalтАЭ one: Indra is by definition the one deserving of / derivationally associated with the sacrifice, and therefore he is the one who should aid it.

English translation:

тАЬThe worshipper, by his conservatory sacrifice, has made Indra present; may Ibring him to my presence to obtain new wealth, him who has been exalted by praise, whether ancient, medieval, or recent.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

With the sacrifice as aid I (previously) brought Indra nearby with his aid. May I turn him hither for newer favor,
him who was strengthened by previous praises, who by midmost ones and by the present ones.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The reciprocity expressed by complementary verbal forms to тИЪav found in the 2nd half of the last vs. is here wrapped up in one word, the instr. ├бvas─Б, which I tr.

twice: I use the aid provided by the sacrifice (cf. 12d) to bring Indra here with his aid (cf. 12c). In GeldnerтАЩs tr. it is only IndraтАЩs aid, but he allows for the other possibility in n.

13a. Renou and Witzel Got┼Н also associate it only with Indra. Given the balanced expression of 12cd, I think it is meant to have a double reading.

Griffith

With sacrifice and wish have I brought Indra; still for new blessings may I turn him hither,
Him magnified by ancient songs and praises, by lauds of later time and days yet recent.

Geldner

Durch das Opfer habe ich fr├╝her den Indra samt seiner Hilfe hierher gebracht. Zu neuer Huld m├╢chte ich ihn herlenken, der sich an den fr├╝heren Preisliedern erbaut hat, der an den mittleren und neuesten.

Grassmann

Durch Lied und Opfer schafft’ ich her den Indra, zu neuer Gunst will ich ihn herw├дrts wenden, Der kr├дftig ward durch alte Lobges├дnge, durch mittlere und durch die allerneusten.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen the thought of glorifying Indra entered my mind, then I gave birth (to his praises); may I laud him before encountering distant (evil) days, whereby he may guide us beyond sin; for those on both sides of us invoke him, as (those on either bank of a river hail) a passenger in a boat.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

She labored when she begot me [=poet]тАФthe Holy Place [=Earth? ritual ground?]. I shall praise Indra before the decisive day,
so that at that time he (will) carry us across (to the far shore) of
constraint, as if with a boat. Both (sides) call upon him as he travels.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The standard tr. (see also K├╝mmel 186) take the two verbs viv├йс╣гa and jaj─Б╠Бna as parallel in the y├бd clause, with m─Б obj. of the first and possibly of the 2nd. I prefer to take viv├йс╣гa as the main clause verb, followed by the y├бd clause, whose (sole) verb is jaj─Б╠Бna. viv├йс╣гa then owes its accent to its initial position in the p─Бda. This interpr.

allows m─Б to take a more natural place, and it also saves us from positing a personal object to viv├йс╣гa, which otherwise is not so construed. (Note that K├╝mmelтАЩs second tr. of this passage [p. 502] is entirely different from his first: he distributes the clauses as I do, but takes viv├йс╣гa as first sg.) And what does it all mean? In my view the dhiс╣г├бс╣З─Б тАШholy placeтАЩ is here the ritual ground, and she is credited with the тАЬbirthтАЭ of the poet qua poet. After this birth, the poet can produce the praise of Indra that he is credited with in p─Бda b, and this in turn leads to the good results in p─Бda c.

P─Бda c contains two different subordinators, y├бtra тАШwhere, whenтАЩ and y├бth─Б тАШso thatтАЩ, with a single verb, subjunctive p─лparat. GeldnerтАЩs explan., that we simply have a doubling of relatives, seems to me the best account; this is reflected, more or less, by OldenbergтАЩs тАЬwo (und) wie тАж,тАЭ though Oldenberg goes on to suggest a complex crossing of two different constructions, which seems over-elaborate. In the published translation I have rendered y├бtra as a temporal adv. (тАЬat that timeтАЭ) with no subordinating force, since I think y├бth─Б expresses purpose and controls the subjunctive.

Rather than taking ├бс╣Гhasaс╕е as an ablative, with most others, I supply p─Бr├бm тАШfar shoreтАЩ, a word related to p─Б╠Бrya- in p─Бda b and to the verb p─лp├бrat itself, and found in this context elsewhere; cf. II.33.3 p├бrс╣гi с╣Зaс╕е p─Бr├бm ├бс╣Гhasaс╕е. Here as well ├бс╣Гhasaс╕е is then a gen. dependent on *p─Бr├бm. Although it unfortunately involves a breach of the p─Бda boundary, I also take n─Бv├йva with the preceding p─Бda, because this simile is almost entirely limited to passages containing verbal forms to тИЪpс╣Ы (I.46.7, 97.7, 99.1, V.4.9, 25.9, VIII.16.11, 18.17, IX.70.10). I also find it hard to imagine Indra traveling by boat, even metaphorically.

Griffith

I have brought forth a song when longing seized me: ere the decisive day will I laud Indra;
Then may lie safely bear us over trouble, as in a ship, when both sides invocate him.

Keith

That to which Dhisana impelled me have I produced;
I shall praise Indra before the decisive day;
Him that goeth as with a ship
Both parties invoke that there he may rescue us.

Geldner

Wenn die Dhisana mich erf├╝llt, neu geboren hat, will ich den Indra vor dem entscheidenden Tage preisen, auf da├Я er uns an diesem aus der Not heraushelfe. Ihn rufen beide Teile an wie den zu Schiffe Fahrenden.

Grassmann

Wenn mich der Trunk ergriffen und erregt hat, dann preis’ ich Indra vor dem Tag der Hauptschlacht, Dass aus der Noth er uns hin├╝berfahre, wie auf dem Schiff; ihn rufen beide Schlachtreih’n.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe vase is filled for him (with Soma); welcome Indra; I pour it out for you to drink, as a water-carrier (pours water) from his bag; may the grateful Soma flow in reverence round Indra for his exhilaration.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

His (soma) tub is filledтАФhail! As a man pours out a bucket, I have poured (for him) to drink.
And the dear soma drinks have together turned him here with
respectful circumambulation, to exhilarate Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The agent noun s├йktar-, which forms an etymological figure with sisice, presumably refers to a habitual or practiced тАШpourerтАЩ. So Tichy (-tar-stems, 159, fld.

by K├╝mmel 570). I have taken k├│┼Ыam as the obj. in the simile rather than the frame, contra the standard tr., though it could certainly go in the frame or in both without appreciably affecting the sense.

The pf. form lacks retroflexion on its root initial, as does one of the other two forms of this pf. in the RV (sisicuс╕е II.24.4), as opposed to expected siс╣гicatuс╕е in VIII.33.13. I have no explanation for the lack of retroflexion.

Griffith

Full is his chalice: Glory! Like a pourer I have filled up the vessel for his drinking.
Presented on the right, dear Soma juices have brought us Indra, to rejoice him, hither.

English translation:

тАЬInvoked of many, the deep ocean arrests you not, nor do the accompanying mountains (stay you); and therefore, summoned by your friends, you have repressed the strong flame abiding in the abyss.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

You have repressed the strong flame: dс╣Ыс╕╖ham cid arujo gavyam ┼лrvam = prabalam api avate vartam─Бnam ┼лrv─Бnalam samyagabh─Бс╣Еkс╣г─лс╕е, you have entirely broken the strong (┼лrva) fire abiding in the deep

Jamison Brereton

Not the deep river nor the surrounding peaks could obstruct you, much-invoked one,
when impelled just so from your comrades, Indra, you broke into the cattle enclosure though it was firmly fastened.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On varanta see comm. ad vs. 9.

Geldner (fld. by Witzel Got┼Н) takes s├бkhibhyaс╕е as a dat. of benefit, but I think it more likely that itтАЩs an ablative with agentival force. See Renou, who simply tr. it as an agent.

The mythological episode is surely the Aс╣ЕgirasesтАЩ energetic help to Indra in the breaking of Vala.

Griffith

Not the deep-flowing flood, O Much-invoked One! not hills that compass thee about restrain thee,
Since here incited, for thy friends, O Indra, thou breakest e’en the firm built stall of cattle.

Geldner

Nicht hielten dich der tiefe Strom, noch die Felsen, die im Wege standen, auf, du Vielgerufener, als du darum zur Eile getrieben f├╝r die Freunde die doch so fest verschlossene Rinderh├╢hle erbrachst, o Indra.

Grassmann

Nicht hielt dich auf das tiefe Meer, nicht Felsen, auch wenn sie dich umschlossen, vielgerufner, So oft du eilend deinen Freunden, Indra, den festverschlossnen Stall der K├╝he aufbrachst.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬWe invoke for our protection the opulent Indra, distinguished in this combat, the leader in the food-bestowing (strife), hearing (our praises), terrible in battles, the destroyer of foes, the conqueror of wealth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

тАУ For blessing we would invoke bounteous Indra, most manly, at this raid, at the winning of the prize of victory,
the strong one who listens, (we would invoke) for help in battles, him who smashes obstacles, the winner of prizes.

Griffith

Call we on Maghavan, auspicious Indra, best Hero in this fight where spoil is gathered,
The Strong who listens, who gives aid in battles, who slays the Vrtras, wins and gathers riches.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ ! рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧ (рдКрддрдпреЗ) рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдЖрджрд┐ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рд╕рдорддреНрд╕реБ) рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ (рдШреНрдирдиреНрддрдореН) рдирд╛рд╢ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рдЙрдЧреНрд░рдореН) рддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡рдпреБрдХреНрдд (рдзрдирд╛рдирд╛рдореН) рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ (рд╕рдЮреНрдЬрд┐рддрдореН) рдФрд░ рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдУрдВ рдХреЛ рдЬреАрддрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐) рд╕реБрд╡рд░реНрдг рдЖрджрд┐ рдзрдиреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рд╢реГрдгреНрд╡рдиреНрддрдореН) рд╕реБрдирддреЗ рд╣реБрдП рдХреЛ (рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН) рдЗрд╕ (рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╕рд╛рддреМ) рдзрди рдФрд░ рдЕрдиреНрди рдЖрджрд┐ рдХреЗ рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рдЧ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рднрд░реЗ) рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдо рдореЗрдВ (рдиреГрддрдордореН) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЛрддреНрддрдо (рдордШрд╡рд╛рдирдореН) рдкрд░рдо рдзрдирд╡рд╛рди рдФрд░ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдореН) рджреБрд╖реНрдЯ рдЬрдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдирд╛рд╢рдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╛ рдХреЛ (рд╣реБрд╡реЗрдо) рдкреБрдХрд╛рд░реИрдВ рдФрд░ рдЙрд╕рдХреЗ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧ рд╕реЗ (рд╢реБрдирдореН) рд╕реБрдЦ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрд╡реЗрдВ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕рдХреА рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐ рдХрд░рдХреЗ рдЖрдк рд▓реЛрдЧ рднреА рдЗрд╕рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдВ реерезренрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рдЬреЛ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдЖрджрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдзрд╛рди рдкреБрд░реБрд╖, рд░рд╛рдЬрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдореЗрдВ рдЪрддреБрд░, рдпреЛрджреНрдзрд╛, рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдзреАрд╢ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЛрдВ, рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЩреНрд╡рд┐рд╡рд╛рдХреЛрдВ (рд╡рдХреАрд▓реЛрдВ) рдФрд░ рд╕реЗрд╡рдХ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╕рддреНрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рдХреЗ рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдг рдХрд░реЗрдВ, рддреЛ рдЙрди рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдУрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╕рджреИрд╡ рд╡рд┐рдЬрдп рдпрд╢ рдХреАрд░реНрддреНрддрд┐ рдФрд░ рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдп рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ реерезренрее рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╕реЛрдо, рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп, рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рдФрд░ рдмрд┐рдЬреБрд▓реА рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдг рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рдХрд░рдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдЗрд╕рд╕реЗ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рдпрд╣ рдмрддреНрддреАрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рдЧреНрдпрд╛рд░рд╣рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ рдпрдерд╛ рд╡рдпрдореВрддрдпреЗ рд╕рдорддреНрд╕реБ рдШреНрдирдиреНрддрдореБрдЧреНрд░рдВ рдзрдирд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╕рдЮреНрдЬрд┐рддрдВ рд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рд╢реГрдгреНрд╡рдиреНрддрдорд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╕рд╛рддреМ рднрд░реЗ рдиреГрддрдордВ рдордШрд╡рд╛рдирдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдВ рд╣реБрд╡реЗрдо рддрддреНрд╕рдЩреНрдЧреЗрди рд╢реБрдирдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдпрд╛рдо рддрдереИрддрдВ рд╕реНрддреБрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдпреВрдпрдордкреНрдпреЗрддрддреНрдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдд реерезренрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╢реБрдирдореН) рд╕реБрдЦрдореНред рд╢реБрдирдорд┐рддрд┐ рд╕реБрдЦрдирд╛режред рдирд┐рдШрдВреж рейред ремред (рд╣реБрд╡реЗрдо) рдЖрд╣реНрд╡рдпреЗрдо (рдордШрд╡рд╛рдирдореН) рдкрд░рдордзрдирд╡рдиреНрддрдореН (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдореН) рджреБрд╖реНрдЯрд╡рд┐рджрд╛рд░рдХрдореН (рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН) (рднрд░реЗ) рд╕рдЩреНрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗ (рдиреГрддрдордореН) рд╢реБрднреИрд░реНрдЧреБрдгреИрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЛрддреНрдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрдореН (рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╕рд╛рддреМ) рдзрдирд╛рдиреНрдирд╛рджрд┐рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рдЬрдХреЗ (рд╢реГрдгреНрд╡рдиреНрддрдореН) (рдЙрдЧреНрд░рдореН) рддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡рдореН (рдКрддрдпреЗ) рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рдп (рд╕рдорддреНрд╕реБ) рд╕рдЩреНрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗрд╖реБ (рдШреНрдирдиреНрддрдореН) рд╣рдиреНрддрд╛рд░рдореН (рд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐) рд╕реБрд╡рд░реНрдгрд╛рджреАрдирд┐ рдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ред рд╡реГрддреНрд░рдорд┐рддрд┐ рдзрдирдирд╛режред рдирд┐рдШрдВреж реиред резрежред (рд╕рдЮреНрдЬрд┐рддрдореН) рд╕рдореНрдпрдЧреНрдЬрд┐рддрд╛рдГ рд╢рддреНрд░рд╡реЛ рдпреЗрди рддрдореН (рдзрдирд╛рдирд╛рдореН) рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдореН реерезренрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГред рдпрджрд┐ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рджрдпреЛрд╜рдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рд╛ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдХреБрд╢рд▓рд╛рдиреНрдпреЛрджреНрдзреДрдиреН рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдзреАрд╢рд╛рдиреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдбреНрд╡рд┐рд╡рд╛рдХрд╛рдиреНрд╕реЗрд╡рдХрд╛рдБрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рддреНрдХреГрддреНрдп рд╕рдЩреНрдЧреГрд╣реНрдгреАрдпреБрд╕реНрддрд░реНрд╣рд┐ рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╕рджреИрд╡ рд╡рд┐рдЬрдпрдГ рдХреАрд░реНрддрд┐рд░реИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдВ рдЪ рдЬрд╛рдпрдд рдЗрддрд┐ реерезренрее рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╕реЛрдордордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд╛рддреНрд░рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореЗрдХрд╛рджрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рдЬреЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рд╡рдЧреИрд░реЗ рдореБрдЦреНрдп рдкреБрд░реБрд╖, рд░рд╛рдЬрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреЗрдд рдЪрддреБрд░, рдпреЛрджреНрдзрд╛, рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдзреАрд╢, рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЩрд╡рд┐рд╡рд╛рдХ (рд╡рдХреАрд▓) рд╡ рд╕реЗрд╡рдХрд╛рдВрдЪрд╛ рд╕рддреНрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд рд╡ рддреНрдпрд╛рдВрдЪрд╛ рд╕реНрд╡реАрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд, рддреЗрд╡реНрд╣рд╛ рддреНрдпрд╛ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдВрдирд╛ рд╕рджреИрд╡ рд╡рд┐рдЬрдп, рдпрд╢, рдХреАрд░реНрддреА рд╡ рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдп рдорд┐рд│рддреЗ. рее резрен рее
